<p><a href="https://stackoverflow.blog/2021/02/16/level-up-mastering-statistics-with-python/?utm_source=Iterable&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_campaign=the_overflow_newsletter"><strong>Level Up: Mastering statistics with Python</strong></a>&nbsp;<em>stackoverflow.blog</em><br>We are kicking off our new Level Up series on the blog with an 8 part module based on Codecademy’s ‘Master Statistics with Python’ taught by Sophie Sommer. Watch on-demand or join the future live sessions – for free!</p>



<p><a href="https://stackoverflow.blog/2021/02/19/podcast-314-how-do-digital-nomads-pay-their-taxes/?utm_source=Iterable&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_campaign=the_overflow_newsletter"><strong>Podcast 313: How do digital nomads pay their taxes?&nbsp;</strong></a>&nbsp;<em>stackoverflow.blog</em><br>As many tech companies go permanently remote, wandering developers will have to consider the implications for taxes, patents, and salaries.</p>



<p><a href="https://blog.pusher.com/realtime-results-election-washington-post/?utm_source=so_newsletter&amp;utm_medium=case_study&amp;utm_campaign=washpost_live_res"><strong>Serving critical realtime updates to news readers using WebSockets</strong></a>&nbsp;<em>promotion</em><br>In November 2020 The Washington Post broke realtime records with a WebSocket implementation which sent 1 million messages per second to global browsers. Read about how they served critical live updates to global readers during the US election.</p>
